Ministry of Education Explains Matters Regarding Educational Associations 169

The Ministry of Education, in order to clarify the use of "report" and telegrams by educational associations when communicating with education bureaus, has issued a directive to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities.

Recently, the Jilin Provincial Education Department forwarded a telegram from Panshi County stating that the old regulations for educational associations stipulated that county educational associations were subordinate to the education bureau. The newly promulgated Educational Association Law stipulates that county educational associations are supervised by the county government. The telegram asks whether communications from the provincial educational association to the education bureau should be changed to official letters for compliance. The Ministry has investigated and found that Article 10 of the Educational Association Law stipulates that the supervisory bodies for county educational associations and their subordinate district educational associations are the county government. However, the county education bureau is part of the government organization and, when necessary, may supervise the county educational association and its district educational associations on behalf of the county government. Communications between them should still use "report" except for instructions. This directive is hereby issued for your information and for transmission to your subordinates. The Ministry of Education (seal). Furthermore, although the Ministry of Education ordered that educational associations be established by the end of March, due to changes in the organization and reorganization methods, the deadline has been extended. Some provinces and cities have not yet fully organized and established their educational associations, and the Ministry of Education continues to receive requests for clarification of doubts from various provinces and cities. The following is a summary of the key points: (1) Can county educational association officers mutually elect one person as a standing officer? The Educational Association Law does not explicitly stipulate or restrict this. For the sake of convenience, it should be permissible for the officers to mutually elect one person as a standing officer. Similarly, district and municipal educational associations may follow the example of county educational associations and have their officers mutually elect a standing officer, and this should be stipulated in the association's constitution to ensure uniformity. (2) Places that have not been designated as cities by the state in accordance with Article 4 of the Municipal Organization Law and do not have a municipal government may not establish municipal educational associations. (3) Teachers and staff of public and private schools at all levels and personnel of educational institutions in provincial capitals may join the district educational associations within the county where the provincial capital is located as members.

Zhejiang Province Holds Educational Design Committee Meeting 170

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education held its first Educational Design Committee meeting at 9:00 AM on the 8th in the department's auditorium. Attendees included Yu Ziyi, Yu Qingtang, Meng Xiancheng, Zheng Xiaocang, Tan Xihong, Li Ximou, Fu Baochen, Yang Baokang, Luo Yun, Xie Yun, Wei Songtang, Ye Suzhong, Xu Shaodi, Xiang Dingrong, Zhang Daoshen, Shen Fubao, Qian Jiazhi, Xiong Wenmin, Luo Dixian, Zhao Mian, Zhang Yiyang, Zhang Xingjian, and Zhang Rentian. Observers included Hu Mengzi, Fang Zuzhen, Zhao Yuren, Zhao Yuyu, and Sun Fuhou. Zhang Daofan chaired the meeting. After the usual formalities, Zhang Daofan gave an opening speech, stating that education is a public undertaking related to the construction of the party and the nation. It is necessary to solicit opinions from people outside the department who are well-versed in various educational issues and jointly discuss solutions in order to integrate and develop the whole. This meeting, if successful, will, on a small scale, provide substantial solutions to various educational problems in Zhejiang Province, and on a large scale, provide a reference for the educational situation in this province for the entire country to consider. He earnestly requested that all gentlemen report and discuss their daily thoughts and the needs and actual situation of education in Zhejiang Province, express their high opinions, and jointly promote the cause of education. Next, Shen Fuzhai reported on the content of the committee's proposed plans, which were originally divided into eleven groups. However, due to time constraints, the focus of the discussions will be on the secondary education group, the education funding group, and the social education group. Other areas, such as primary education, vocational education, and women's education, will also be discussed to improve them. It was proposed that the schedule be as follows: On the morning of the first day, the group method for all agenda items will be decided. In the afternoon and on the morning of the second day, group meetings will be held. On the third day, based on the results of the group meetings, a plenary meeting will be held to make final overall decisions. The group meetings then began, and it was decided to divide the groups into secondary education, social education, and education funding. Each person was responsible for deciding which group to join. As a result, the secondary education group consisted of ten people: Meng Xiancheng, Xiong Wenmin, Zheng Xiaocang, Li Ximou, Yu Ziyi, Luo Yun, Yang Baokang, Tan Xihong, Shen Fuzhai, and Xie Xue. The social education group consisted of five people: Fu Hezhen, Yu Qingtang, Zhao Mian, Zhang Rentian, and Ye Suzhong. The education funding group consisted of seven people: Wei Songtang, Qian Jiazhi, Zhang Xingjian, Luo Dixian, Xiang Dingrong, Xu Shaodi, and Zhang Yiyang. The secondary education group had fourteen proposals, the social education group had five proposals, and the education funding group had five proposals. The plenary meeting discussed these matters until noon, when it was temporarily adjourned. Group meetings began in the afternoon. (This report is from our local correspondent.)

Shanghai Middle School Affiliated Elementary School Reports on Elementary School Curriculum Standards 171

Results of Experimentation

The Shanghai Middle School Affiliated Elementary School of Jiangsu Province on Shangwen Road in this city has always been very interested in experimentation and research in new education. This time, the Ministry of Education issued a notice to all provinces to quickly report the results of the trial implementation of the "Provisional Standards for Primary and Secondary School Curricula" for the Ministry of Education's reference in revising these standards. Upon receiving the order, the school immediately reported the school's research and experimentation process for these curriculum standards. The original report is excerpted below. The school's experimentation and research on the provisional standards for the primary school curriculum was conducted in three aspects: First, based on the teaching experience of the school's colleagues, detailed criticisms were made. Second, the current primary school textbooks for each subject were analyzed and compared with the provisional curriculum standards to carefully examine their gains and losses. Third, scientific methods were used to test whether the teaching methods introduced by the provisional curriculum standards were consistent with reality. After three semesters of experimentation and research, some gains were made. The following is a summary of the key points of the assignments and teaching methods: 1. Regarding the key points of assignments for each subject: (1) In the third and fourth grades of the Chinese language writing class, the item of learning simplified cursive script should be deleted. The reason is that the children's regular script performance in the third and fourth grades is poor, and it is feared that practicing cursive script will further reduce their regular script progress. (2) In the fifth and sixth grades of the social studies class, an item on career guidance should be added. The reason is that, according to the actual situation, few primary school graduates continue their education, and most of them find employment, so it is appropriate to implement career guidance to prepare them for employment. (3) In the fifth and sixth grades of the arithmetic class, an item on the recognition and calculation of various simple bills should be added. The reason is that this material is necessary for social life. (4) In the third and fourth grades of the arithmetic class, an item on the recognition of Roman numerals and tally marks should be added. The reason is that these numbers are still commonly used in society. (5) In the first and second grades of the arithmetic class, an item on the nine-nine multiplication table practice for multiplication and division involving zero should be added. The reason is that the provisional curriculum standards only have addition and subtraction nine-nine tables involving zero, but not multiplication and division nine-nine tables involving zero. However, the current arithmetic textbooks have them, so it seems that they can be adopted. 2. Regarding the key points of teaching methods for each subject: (1) In the Chinese language class for senior grades, children can be asked to write diaries. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, practicing expression through diaries is more effective than regular composition assignments. (2) Chinese language composition papers should be carefully graded. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, teachers using grading methods for children's writing exercises are more effective than so-called guidance methods. (3) In Chinese language calligraphy teaching, emphasis should be placed on regular practice. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, children should practice writing regularly rather than opportunistically. (4) In Chinese language reading teaching, children should be asked to memorize short vernacular articles. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, mastering short vernacular articles greatly benefits the understanding and expression of words. (5) The arrangement of teaching materials for the arithmetic class should use a circular method. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, teaching materials arranged using the circular method are more effective. (6) The teaching of arithmetic mental calculation should be based on children's calculation ability and the steps should be properly determined, from easy to complex. The reason is that, according to comparative experimental results, if mental calculation problems are beyond children's calculation ability, their effectiveness will be minimal. In summary, the above are the results of the school's experimentation and research on the provisional curriculum standards, and are matters not yet discussed in these standards. Other matters, such as the application of inductive methods in the teaching of arithmetic principles, the focus on facts in arithmetic propositions, and the emphasis on stroke order guidance in calligraphy teaching, are the results of the school's teaching experiments and are consistent with the provisional curriculum standards, so they will not be discussed in detail. Only those that are not included in the standards are listed above for your review and transmission to the Ministry of Education.

Shanghai International Boy Scout Performance 172

The Jewish Boy Scouts' "Shanghai Architecture" Wins

The Chinese Jinan University Team's "Mutual Aid" Wins Applause from the Entire Audience

According to the Guomin News Agency, the annual meeting of the International Boy Scouts of this city was held at 2:30 PM on the 6th at the Millington Field on Hongqiao Road. Over 400 people participated, including the representative of the municipal department, Tong Xingbai (represented by Wang Gang), representatives of the municipal Boy Scout Council, Wang Gang, Zhang Xunfang, and Shen Yu, representatives of the Boy Scout Associations of various countries, guests, and others. The performers included Boy Scouts from seven countries. The Chinese Boy Scouts participating were the 64th Troop (Jinan University) and the 221st Troop (Shanghai University). The performances on that day included camping, fire starting, house building, dressing, rescue, flag signals, martial arts, and many other activities. As a result of the judging, the Jewish team won and received three silver shields presented by the Municipal Boy Scout Council, the Rotary Club, and the former British Consul General. The 64th Chinese Boy Scout Troop received a New Moon Shield from the Bunnemann Company. Finally, Wang Gang, the representative of the municipal department, and Millington, the British Consul General, delivered speeches in their respective national languages. The performances of the Chinese and Jewish teams are excerpted below.

The Chinese Team (Jinan University) performed a piece entitled "Mutual Aid". Several dozen Boy Scouts, dressed as people from various countries, including farmers, merchants, soldiers, were painted on their hands, feet, and faces in various colors, including red, black, and white, and wore tattered clothes of various colors. They first walked and danced around the field for a week, and then performed Boy Scout activities such as rescue, flag signals, stacking, and various games. The performance expressed the spirit of love among all nations through mutual aid. The performance was quite humorous and interesting, and won a lot of applause from the audience. The Jewish team performed a piece entitled "Shanghai Architecture". First, they erected a five-legged archway with the flags of seven countries attached to the table. In the middle was a horizontal picture of the Shanghai Bund from twenty years ago. Then, they stacked some high-rise buildings on the return trip, and added several warships to the Huangpu River, just like the Bund scenery of today. Although this performance was original, the deep meaning of flattering the aggression of various countries against China made our hair stand on end. Can we not regard this as a great shame? We sincerely hope that the people of the country will rise up to avenge it.

The County Education Bureau Held Its First Meeting of the People's Education Committee Yesterday 173

The Shanghai County Education Bureau held its first meeting of the People's Education Committee yesterday afternoon. The attendees were Zhang Yi, Zhu Hange, Lin Qing, Zheng Yi, Niu Zhiyi, Jin Zuobin, Zheng Shaoyuan, Yao Huiquan, Shi She, and Yang Huiming. The chairman was Shi She, the recorder was Yan Zhongguang. After the usual formalities, the reports were briefly presented. Next, the discussion items were: (1) How should the design for popularizing literacy education in this county be designed? It was resolved to adopt the principle of popularization by year, with separate three-year, funding, and facility items. Zheng Guozhai, Yang Huiming, Jin Zuobin, and Zheng Shaoyuan were appointed to draft a plan, which will then be submitted to the committee for discussion. (2) How should the implementation of phonetic symbols be drafted? It was resolved to adopt the principle of phased implementation. The Education Bureau will be asked to draft a preliminary plan and then submit it to the committee for discussion. (3) What should be the focus of the people's education movement in this county, and how should it be promoted to increase efficiency? It was resolved to focus on livelihood education and start with guiding cooperation and promoting side businesses. Each social education institution will draft a plan and then submit it to the committee for discussion. (4) What standards should be set for illiterate people in this county in order to facilitate investigation and facilities? It was resolved that the minimum standard for literacy would be the ability to write a simple resume of oneself. (5) Should the basic characters necessary for the people be sorted out and compiled into teaching materials for use in various people's schools? It was resolved that the People's Education Experimental Zone should first collect and sort out materials according to the social conditions of this county and then promote the compilation by staff. (6) Should the length of the school year for rural people's schools be changed based on the current state of people's lives? It was resolved that the Education Bureau should solicit opinions from various people's schools before handling the matter. The meeting was adjourned.

A Glimpse of the Fisheries Exhibition Department 181

— Sun Choucheng

The Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau, recognizing the gradual decline of China's coastal fisheries and the intentional aggression of foreigners, believes that if improvements are not made, the consequences will be unimaginable. Therefore, it has joined forces with the Department of Agriculture and Mining, as well as provincial and municipal party headquarters, to organize a Fisheries Propaganda Association to awaken fellow citizens and jointly seek development. On Sunday, I took time to visit and tour the exhibition department for a week. Here are my observations:

In the main hall of the exhibition department, there is a horizontal banner with the eleven characters "Strive to Complete the Premier's Fisheries Port Plan" hanging. Below it hangs a map of the Premier's Fisheries Port Plan, drawn on a full-width bamboo cloth. Beside it are couplets: "Enrich the sea and develop new strategies, benefit the country and the people, techniques surpass Guan Zhong"; "Maintain the auspicious dream of expansion, care for the masses' well-being, the duty lies with Yu Ren." The four walls are covered with slogans such as "China's import and export of marine products lose more than 20 million taels annually," "The fisheries association is the basic organization of fishermen," "The ocean is an infinite treasure trove," and "Shanghai is the great fishing port of the Orient." The first room displays fish specimens from the Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Experimental Station. There are over a hundred glass bottles of various sizes, all filled with liquid preservatives and tightly sealed. A description is attached to the outside of each bottle, detailing the name in both Chinese and Western languages. On the wall is a chemical composition table of important edible fish (noting moisture, protein, fat, and ash weight), and a table showing the growth rate of farmed fish (divided into freshwater and saltwater, and weight and body length), as well as a table showing the spawning period of important fish (noted by month), one for each. The second room displays shrimp, crabs, snails, and other shellfish. There are candlestick shrimp and bamboo shrimp. There are many types of crabs, called cross crab, shuttle crab, ghost-face crab, shy woman crab, ginkgo crab, three-star crab, and Zhang Fei crab. Some have a shape similar to a shuttle, some have three stars on their backs, some have shells like ghost faces, and some have a shape like Zhang Fei. Generally, they are similar to the "crab-backed beauties" that were widely publicized in Shanghai some time ago. They are named according to their shape and color. The most unusual is the "Red Flag Broadsword Balcony", with claws about six times the length of the body, rarely seen in the market. There are large dog snails and Chang Xin snails. The shellfish is called brocade chicken heart. The third room displays copper crown, eight generations, horseshoe, parrot, and other shells, as well as stone fungus and sea pine. A long table is set up in the middle, displaying specimens of baleen whale, red octopus, sea dragon, seal and various specimens. Huge and unparalleled, with sparkling eyes, lifelike. The fourth room displays marine survey instruments and meteorological measurement instruments. There is also a six-foot square wooden plate with a model of the coastal terrain of Jiangsu made of sand and mud. The fifth room displays nets and fishing gear. There are various types of nets, including Zhang net, pair net, purse seine, tied net, as well as hand-cranked net, air-blown net, Yangcao net, and boat-towing net. There are various types of hooks, including lure hooks, luminous hooks, balance hooks, and standing line hooks. All kinds of shapes are unseen before. There are also various models of fishing boats, some modeled after the latest Japanese styles, and some are the old ones used in our country. They are six or seven feet long or three or four feet long, all with sails raised high and complete machinery, no different from real ships. The sixth room has several colored maps of the sea currents of Jiangsu Province, with detailed annotations. On the table are hundreds of books on fisheries research for anyone to read. There are several other rooms, but they were closed early when the visiting time arrived, so I couldn't visit them all. There is also a gift distribution area, with two large barrels of sea fish. You can get a lottery ticket. Some people who touched fresh yellow croaker smiled. A young woman touched a small yellow croaker and asked to exchange it. There were many jokes. I happened to touch a dried fish and gave it away because it was inconvenient to carry. She left happily.

A Record of the Guangdong Overseas Chinese's "Collecting Gold" 182

— Nuoxia

The term "collecting gold" originally meant holding something of golden color, which is supposed to be a happy event. However, people from Guangdong use it as a euphemism for collecting and storing the bones of their ancestors, turning joy into sorrow. Is there an intention to moderate the emotions? This must be recorded.

When overseas Chinese from Guangdong die in this area, their bodies are mostly buried in the Guangzhao Mountain Villa, west of Gonghe Road in Zhabei. Every five years, there is a "collecting gold" ceremony. The coffin is opened, and the bones are taken out and wiped clean of accumulated dirt with wine. Then, they are neatly arranged and placed in a coffin lid, fumigated with incense sticks, and exposed to sunlight. After drying, they are stored in urns, with ash used to secure the edges. They are either transported back to their hometown or reburied in the soil. This event is usually held during the Qingming and Chongyang festivals, but especially on the day after the Cold Food Festival. Therefore, when you visit the villa at that time, you will see bones along the path, a shocking sight, like a skull exhibition. It is like a dream, making one wonder, "Where are they now?"

A Foreign Monk at Lingyin Temple 183

— Rui Hongchu

Yesterday, my friend Mr. Shen Fengshi came to visit from Hangzhou. We have been friends for ten years, and it was a great joy to meet again after a long separation. That evening, we got drunk at the Huzhou Food Company on Tianjin Road. Mr. Shen told me that there is a foreign monk in Lingyin Temple in Hangzhou who has truly opened a new era for monks. Here is what Mr. Shen said:

A reporter from the American Damei Newspaper, Mr. Qiang He, is thirty-three years old and quite famous in the journalism field. In addition to covering news, he attends the Huaguang Night School for Overseas Chinese to study Chinese. He can recite poems and speaks with a Northern accent. He also has studied Buddhist scriptures and can recite them aloud. He knows that the boundless Buddhist Dharma is the foundation for establishing oneself in the world. He often told his wife, Mary, that he would go abroad to China to enter a temple and practice vegetarianism and worship Buddha for the rest of his life. His wife repeatedly tried to dissuade him. However, Mr. Qiang He went to China alone last March. He visited the abbot of Lingyin Temple in Fangzhou and asked to become a Buddhist disciple. His sincerity moved the abbot, who could not refuse and kept him in the temple. Mr. Qiang He chants scriptures day and night, which sounds pleasant. His achievements are quite impressive. Therefore, visitors to Hangzhou now see a foreign monk in Lingyin Temple, who is Mr. Qiang He.

Don't Confuse West Lake with Fuzhou 184

— Chen Boying

Everyone knows West Lake in Hangzhou. However, few people know about West Lake in Fuzhou, Fujian Province. I am writing this specifically to inform those who like to travel. The lake is located west of Fuzhou City. It was created by Prefect Yan Gao in the third year of the Taikang era of the Jin Dynasty, covering a circumference of more than ten li, for the purpose of irrigating farmland. During the time of Wang Shenzhi, it grew to more than forty li. Later, it gradually became silted up. The lake is surrounded by mountains on three sides, with two islands floating in the middle: Xiaogushan and Xieping Island. They are connected to the mainland by the Feihong Bridge and Buyun Bridge. Entering the lake first passes through Xieping Island. There is the West Lake Thatched Cottage, Baozhong Temple, Chenglan Pavilion, Yanxi Hall, and Yanjing Building. Xiaogushan is located in the northeast, connected by the Feihong Bridge. There is the Wanzaitang, Jinghu Pavilion, Huxin Pavilion, and Jianjia Pavilion on the mountain. There is also the Kaihua Temple, so it is also called Kaihua Island. There are many mountains around the lake, such as Guian Mountain, Elephant Buddha Mountain, Guo Mountain, Bailong Mountain, Meiting Mountain, Wenhua Mountain, Luping Mountain, Dajia Mountain, Lingguang Mountain, Dameng Mountain, Fenghuang Mountain, Qingquan Mountain, Hong Mountain, Huang Mountain, Mo Mountain, Xichan Mountain, Tongpan Mountain, Wufeng Mountain, Dapeng Mountain, Huofeng Mountain, Ma'an Mountain, Yuewang Mountain, Longyao Mountain, Taiping Mountain, Meiliu Mountain, and Wolong Mountain. They cannot all be listed. Famous scenic spots and historical sites include Sanshan Academy, Xie's Thatched Cottage, Guian Well, Yunwo Pond, Dizang Temple, Shanghuwei Bridge, Xiahuwei Bridge, Baofu Temple, Yuquan Temple, Rancuo Gorge Deer Milk Spring, Yiai Pavilion, the former residence of Zheng Yu of the Song Dynasty, the hermitage of Yu Bo'an of the Ming Dynasty, Linshui Villa, Tongxi, the tomb and ancestral hall of Li Zhongding Gong, Lingguang Temple, Jianchi, Yiran Pavilion, West Lake Villa, Zhenwu Palace, Yuxu Hall, Zhu Zi Temple, Pilu Pavilion, Sanyi Temple, Yuancui Pavilion, Lotus Pavilion, Ink Pond, Yanglong Pond, Yujing Pond, Xiangyan Temple, the Great Hui Pagoda Pavilion, Yufeng Pavilion, Cuiwei Hermitage, Hongshan Temple, Sijie Pavilion, Xiyin Temple, Yishan Hall, Taishan Xing Temple, Liu Bridge, Shishan Realm, Lengjia Temple, Huanzhu Nunnery, Beichan Nunnery, Conglu Garden, Qin Pavilion, Xianjing Waterfall, Xuansha Temple Puwen Courtyard, Zhuoxiu Pavilion, etc. There are countless others. As for the scenery, it is said that there are sixteen scenic spots in West Lake: Fairy Bridge Willow Color, Dameng Pine Sound, Ancient Wall Slanting Sun, Crystal First Moon, Lotus Pavilion Evening Singing, Xichan Dawn Bell, Huxin Spring Rain, Chenglan Dawn Oriole, Lake Sky Dragon Boat Racing, Dragon Tongue Tasting Spring, Shengshan Ancient Temple, Feilai Strange Peak, Yishan Eating Lychees, Yanglou Watching the Sea, Lake Pavilion Cultivating Tranquility, and Hongqiao Night Mooring. One can imagine its magnificence. Before entering the lake, you must pass through the Li Zhongding Gong Ancestral Hall, which is dedicated to Li Gang, the Prime Minister of the Song Dynasty. The couplet of the ancestral hall says: "His advance and retreat concerned the country and the people, his heroic spirit forever guards the lakes and mountains." There is also a poem: "The grass and trees around the Prime Minister's Ancestral Hall are barren, his heroic soul forever resents Wang Huang. His life's righteousness was exhausted by hardships, his remains were barely spared after nine deaths. Alas, since the Northerners brought the invading bandits, they have eternally taught the Southerners to feel the vicissitudes of life. Yue Wang died thin, Han Wang was old, the historical records still share the hatred." Behind the ancestral hall is the Lotus Pavilion. The pavilion faces the lake on three sides, and the mountain scenery and water vapor flood the windowsills. In summer, red lotuses bloom, and the fragrance floats on the desk. The acres of blue often reveal delicate red, like fairies in crimson clothes dancing on a green carpet, which is most spectacular. Entering Xieping Island, there is a tall building standing dangerously by the lake, which is the Chenglan Pavilion. Dozens of willows surround it. Every time the grass grows in March, the orioles sing in unison, gentle and melodious, also intoxicating. Passing the Hong Bridge, you arrive at Wanzai Hall. The hall is dedicated to the predecessors of the township who were skilled in poetry. The couplets say: "A few families with mulberry trees on the lakeside, ten miles of hibiscus by the water's edge." "Viewing the water and viewing the mountains are all wonderful realms, the wind and the moon shine through the bright Xuan." "The clouds lie cold on the clothes, the mountain air is beautiful day and night." "Half the city is bright in the evening glow, looking at the staggered battlements, recognizing the home in the countryside, a lake of autumn moon is blue, watching the misty waves, as if one is in Yingzhou." During festivals, poets often gather here. This is the general overview of the lake.

Occasional Talks on Seasonal Items (3) 185

— Tianxu Wosheng

Tao Zhugong said that planting a thousand willow trees can provide enough firewood and charcoal. Li Shizhen said that willow trees can be planted horizontally, vertically, upside down, and in any direction, and they will all grow. Because they are easy to plant and grow quickly, and the branches, leaves, roots, bark, flowers, stamens, and cotton seeds can all be used as medicine, their uses are very extensive. Planting trees during Qingming is most appropriate. Planting willows at the door is probably the same as breaking willows at Yangguan, used as a farewell. It is a reminder that as a guest in a foreign land, how can one make a ten-year plan for planting trees? Planting willows is one of them. The fire taken from elm and willow in spring is precisely because the branches are lush and inexhaustible. Willow charcoal is used as a follow-up agent for yin water. Its power to decolorize and eliminate odors is stronger than bone charcoal. Its ash contains a lot of potassium carbonate, which can be extracted by soaking in water to wash away oil stains and replace soap. Willow branches can also be sharpened into toothbrushes, which are great for picking teeth. Because they are soft, they do not harm the teeth. They also contain salicylic acid, which can treat gum swelling, so they are often used. There are different types of willows. Bulrush willow is also known as water willow. The branches are strong and can be used for arrow shafts. Osier grows by the water, with coarse white leaves. The wood grain is slightly red and can be used for carriage axles. It is not easy to break. Its branches can be used to make boxes and baskets. The West Xixi area of Hangzhou has extremely lush wild growth. The bamboo hats sold in Hushu are made of osier. Mencius referred to it as "bending osier into cups".

I planted willows by the water on Meixue Road. They provided shade even after three years. After seven years, they were taller than the building. Every year around the Qingming festival, the tender sun warms the flowers, and the stamens break into fluff. Forced by the east wind, they gather in the southwest corner of the wall, rolling into balls. They are taken to fill pillows, which are fragrant, soft, and lovely. They are not like kapok, which generates heat and is repulsive. The Ben Cao Fa Ming states that willow catkins can be used to make felt and replace wool for mattresses. They are soft and cool, and suitable for children to sleep on. The Wai Tai Mi Yao states that for gold sores that bleed, sealing them with willow catkins will stop the bleeding. The Jing Yan Fang states that for vomiting blood and coughing up blood, bake and grind willow catkins and take one qian with rice soup. The Pu Ji Fang states that for pus sores on the face, mix willow catkins and powder in equal parts and apply with lamp oil. The Ji Jian Fang states that for those suffering from gonorrhea, boil Qingming willow leaves to make tea until cured. The Zhou Hou Fang states that for malignant sores that cannot be named, wash them frequently with willow leaves or bark, unboiled juice, and a little salt. In addition, there are too many methods to list. It is sufficient to know that the use of willow is very extensive. Breaking willows and planting them outside the door during Qingming is precisely to encourage people to take them away and plant them everywhere.

Travels in India (19) 186

— Linghua

On the sixth day, an Indian monk led a tour of the Balawana Temple and the Nigan Temple Parowanath & Jaima Swetambar Dadaii. The temple is not very large, but it is fresh and beautiful and made entirely of marble. It is attached with a garden and fish pond. Visitors must take off their shoes. There are very few monks inside, but the freshness of the temple proves that it has a great influence in society. The Nigan religion is neither Buddhism nor Hinduism. It is a separate religion, namely the Victory School of Patriarch Qi Nana. Sheng means the highest meaning or is called Ni Jian Zi (same as Qian), which is a different transliteration. Ni Jian Zi was contemporary with the Buddha. There is the Sutra of Buddha Saying Ni Jian Zi's Prophecy. This is a major Mahayana sect that the Buddha allowed at that time. However, according to its source, this ancient sect existed before the Buddha was born. It is very strict in asceticism and prohibits killing. It is said that there are still people raising rats in some places, emphasizing the importance of life as the basis of human life, so they worship motherhood and worship the female reproductive organs as the source of life. This is its special point. There are also many sects. There are many small statues in the temple, but it was too late to see them. According to the Sutra of Ni Jian Zi's Prophecy, it completely understands worldly laws, roughly like the Zhou Li of Confucianism. Those who were brought back to Buddhism by the Buddha are now said by Indians that Ni Jian is also a sect of Buddhism. Its content is not known to those who do not understand Indian writing.

Here, there is something to know. Each country has its own situation. If you travel to India or Rome and deny God, it is like denying God in the United States or denying Marx in Russia. Everything in India cannot be separated from God. Even the polytheism of ancient Greece was influenced by India. From Pythagoras to Plato, they all believed in reincarnation. Pythagoras believed that his previous life was a peacock. According to recent research, Greece was influenced by Buddhism. Not only Greece, but also the polytheism of ancient Judaism, Solomon's thousands of concubines all believed in the Indian polytheistic religion. Even Islam still does not leave polytheism.

Bami told me that there are many mother goddesses in India, and Kali is the greatest. She is the common great mother who protects all living beings. Since the beginning of time, Kali has fought and won against the demon king Asuras, so the people and their descendants have been able to live in peace to this day. There is also the goddess of wisdom, Swarawatio, the goddess of wealth, Laksmi, and Durga, and many others. I think this is similar to Greek mythology, like the female immortals in the Chu Ci of China. However, it is only the material for writing and has nothing to do with superstition. Xin Han Jun also said that the most common Hindu male god is Krishna and the goddess is Durga, because Durga also fought against demons to protect all living beings. The final victory is always with the goddess, which is the same as Kali. The worship of Kali is only in the province of Bengal.

Cotton Market Shows Signs of Instability 192

Hankou Standard Cotton Falls by Six or Seven Qian

Youth Garden

Morning 197

— Luo Xiang

Everything was covered in darkness. The stars were still twinkling with smiles when the alarm clock woke us two from our dreams. Remembering that the English exam, for which we hadn't prepared enough, was today, we disregarded our weariness, which made it hard to even open our eyes, and quickly got out of bed.

Experience told us, "At this time, the person in charge of the water faucets definitely hasn't woken up yet." We had no choice but to hastily wash with the remaining lukewarm water in the overnight thermos. Tiptoeing, we quietly walked down the stairs. Seeing that the dormitory door was still securely locked, we climbed out the window to the classroom and turned on the lights to study English.

The short hand on the wall clock had gradually moved to the middle of six and seven o'clock. The sky had changed from the color of a fish's belly to bright daylight. After we had read through the English once, we felt hungry. We decided to go outside the school to buy something to fill our stomachs.

Walking to the school gate, we saw that it wasn't open yet. The old gatekeeper was still having sweet dreams in bed. We leaned against the gate and knocked loudly, as if someone were knocking outside the school. After a while, we heard the sound of spitting phlegm, dragging slippers, and mumbling complaints from the next room. The old gatekeeper came out wearing his clothes. We quickly hid in a dark corner, watching as the old man asked who it was, while unlocking the gate. He walked out of the school gate and saw that there was no one there. He said to himself, "There's no one here. Could it be that my own ears are playing tricks on me, disturbing people's sleep? But now..." He turned back to look at the clock in the room, "But now it's almost seven o'clock, and the school gate should be open." He opened the gate wider and walked back inside. Lan and I suppressed our laughter, quietly watching him. At this point, we quickly jumped out of the school gate. Outside the school, we couldn't hold back our laughter anymore.

Perhaps it was because of the spring weariness that, although it was already past six o'clock, there was no one on the road except for the coolies who got up early for a living. The doors of the shops on both sides were still tightly closed. We wandered for a long time. As we turned the corner at the intersection of Dalian Road, we suddenly saw wisps of white smoke coming out of a chimney next to the road. We rushed over. It was a small noodle shop. An old woman was cooking noodles in the steam. There were a few tables in the middle. Three people, looking like coolies, were eating heartily.

"What?" I couldn't help but hesitate. I turned my head to ask Lan.

"Let's go. I'm very hungry. Let's not have class prejudices."

We resolutely walked in and chose a table by the wall to sit down. The old woman hurried over and said earnestly, "The shop is small and narrow. To think that young ladies like you would come here. Are you here for noodles?"

"Yes, two bowls."

She hurriedly went to cook the noodles and carefully washed the bowls and chopsticks several times.

"If a reporter from a small newspaper came here, there would be another news item in tomorrow's newspaper—'Female students eat noodles in a small noodle shop'," I said to Lan while eating.

After finishing the noodles, we went to pay the bill. It was only twenty copper coins. We paid a dime and walked out. The old woman quickly called out, "There's more."

"It's alright."

The old woman sent our backs disappearing into the morning light with a look of surprise and joy, still saying thank you.

"If we ate a meal at a famous restaurant, even if we gave them several dimes, they wouldn't be satisfied. But now, it's just a few copper coins, and the old woman is already very happy."

"This is because desires increase with the environment," Lan said.

Walking into the school, the old gatekeeper was sitting and smoking. Seeing me coming in, he asked, "Did you young ladies stay outside the school last night? You came so early today."

We had no choice but to suppress our laughter and mumbled a response.

Going to School 198

— Lan Zhu

Hong, please imagine how excited and earnestly I read your letter. My trembling heart and soul, amidst the mingling of blood and tears, were like a broken string fluttering in a gale.

The tone of my life is still played as it was in the past, but my wandering state of mind changes constantly. I am constantly floating and sinking in a whirlpool of suffering. Hong, you say my emotions are fragile and too capricious. That is indeed a piercing remark. I don’t know why, but even a slightly unsatisfactory event will make me secretly shed tears behind others’ backs. I remember one morning, receiving a registered letter from you, saying you were sick in a foreign land. I hadn't even finished reading it when I felt a sharp pain in my heart, and tears welled up. Finally, I lay on my pillow and cried to my heart's content, until class was over. Hui came into the dormitory, and I reluctantly held back my tears, pretending to be sick to parry their probing inquiries. Hong, it seemed like they knew all along, and a cold sneer appeared on each of their faces. Hong, I wished there was a hole I could drill into and escape. I couldn't bear their kind of humiliation. I was truly embarrassed then. Hong, I don't know how many times I have experienced such small tragedies. When will I ever be free?

Sometimes, thinking of life’s journey, it feels as though twilight is rapidly approaching. My feet are wounded by thorns, and I can no longer move forward. It is as if there are ferocious beasts closing in. Hong, you flew in from beyond the sky, rescuing this weakling who was approaching death. I am gaining new life under your care.

Beloved Hong, I am so grateful for your earnest guidance. First, clear away the atmosphere of sorrow, overcome the floating-duckweed-like consciousness; second, devote all your energy to studying. Hong, this is indeed the path that young people should take at this stage. In recent years, the surge of revolutionary tides has swept many young people out of schools, causing them to sink deeply into the whirlpool of the times. Now, they feel emptiness from reality. Every young person is spreading in this morbid state. Where to go? This question is now widely circulating among young people. Indeed, modern young people are still wandering on the wrong path in life. In particular, the matter of dropping out of school causes them to wander, and because of wandering, they have no way to solve the problem of living, eventually leading to suicide. We can see these tragic facts everywhere.

In this poor and lacking China, it is certainly not easy to find a way to live. However, the youth themselves lack the skills to make a living, which is also a major reason. If they had true scientific knowledge, it would be very needed in this China that is being built. Hong, I feel this way now.

Hong, your love of literature is certainly your personality, but your environment also forces you to step onto the literary field. I still remember in a long letter you gave me last winter, you said, "Zhu, wandering on the impoverished road of life, literature is my only comfort." Hong, this is precisely the phenomenon that young people who feel spiritual distress must have. You are just one of them. Recently, many young people have neglected proper science and are intoxicated in the garden of literature, especially young people who have fallen behind on the journey of life. They use literature to sing of their hearts full of sorrow. Alas, this uninspiring scene is a terrible temptation for young people to fall into a bottomless abyss.

Hong, your year of wandering the world's sorrows has been secretly revealed in the letters you gave me. Spending your time so emptily like you, the vague future is even more vague. I hope you start student life again, even though this is a widespread and serious problem of dropping out of school.

Strive hard, break out of the pincer attack. Hong, I am waiting for you.

Go to school.

Peace of Mind 199

— Jun Zhe

Brother De, it has been a long, long time since we have seen him. De is a very hardworking person, and his school is also a strict school like a church school. We all know this deeply. However, even so, we cannot help but have doubts, because we do not believe that in this period of nearly two months, he has not even come to see us once, nor even had the time to write us a letter. So, we have gone from suspicion to anxiety. The idea of going to see him, I don’t know how many times and how many days it has arisen, but after all, we are all people with duties in our bodies, and because the location of his school is in such a remote West Shanghai, therefore we have no chance to fulfill our wishes. Yesterday, we heard that his school had started spring break. At the same time, my sister, Chun Di, little sister and I decided to go to Ye Family Garden today, so I thought of seeing Brother De first today, and calling him to play with us.

Early this morning, Chun Di got up. While he was washing his hands and face, he urged me like this, saying:

—Jun, you should get up too. It takes two hours to go to Wusong from here. If you are late, I am afraid Brother De will be out again.

Oh, yes. Although it is only thirty or forty miles from here to Wusong, it does take two hours to go by train. Here, we cannot but thank our road administration authorities. Hearing Chun Di's words, which seemed to contain a warning, I hurriedly rolled out of bed, hastily washed my hands and face, and started to go to the train station.

Things turned out to be so unfortunate. As I stepped into the station gate, I only heard a "woo" sound. The train to Wusong had slowly pulled out of the platform. Oh, I could only stare at its gradually disappearing back and the black smoke still lingering in the air, quietly waiting for the next train, which was an hour away.

"A day is like a year," I think this sentence is most appropriate to describe my state of mind when I was waiting for the train at the station.

Thank goodness, the train to Wusong that I was eagerly waiting for finally arrived. So I rushed into the carriage as if someone who had fallen into a deep well had suddenly seen someone taking a rope to rescue him. Soon, with a "woo" sound, the train started. It wound its way through many villages and fields, but I did not take in all these beautiful spring suburbs, because at this time, I was only thinking about whether Brother De was doing well at home, and how I would make him welcome my unexpected visit.

—People often return with the opposite of what they hope for. I forgot who it was, but it seemed like someone had said this to me. Now, of course, I returned with the opposite of what I hoped for, because when I arrived at Brother De's school, after inquiring from his roommates, I learned that Brother De had gone on a trip to Fort Baoshan with a group of them and their German professor. So I had to hang my head dejectedly and left this message back:

"Brother De, I came full of excitement, to see you, and fully expected to go to Ye's Family Garden with you, but who knew that on the way back, there would only be a desolate me? Today I can no longer muster the interest to go sightseeing, and I also believe that they—my sister and Chun Di, etc.—will all have the same degree of disappointment as me. But even so, this visit of mine cannot be considered a wasted trip, because from the fact that you can go on a trip to Fort Baoshan, I know that our previous guess that you were sick, or that you had some special accident, has been disproven by the facts, letting us know that we were a little neurotic. In this way, although we cannot meet today, we can all put our unsettled minds at ease. Now I am leaving, I wish you good health and progress.

Month × Day × Jun's note,"

Youth Garden

Random Notes of a Northern Trip 200

— Anping

V. Xuanwu Lake at Night

The Temple of the City God and the Central Party Headquarters are very close. After dismounting, I went to find Hao. It was already quite dark. Without taking a moment's rest, Hao took us to dinner. Hao said that the best place to go was the Confucius Temple. The Confucius Temple, that place, is truly an old friend of mine. But the fatigue that came from riding a horse made me not want to take another step. I said, "Forget it." So he led us to a Cantonese restaurant. I remember that six or seven years ago, Dingjiaqiao was truly desolate. But now, there were actually several decent restaurants. Speaking of that day's dinner, it was really not very good. But this "not very good" refers to the restaurant, not the host. Not to mention that the host treated me to dinner, even if he treated me to a big pancake, it wouldn't matter at all.

After dinner, I said that I wanted to take a walk on Xuanwu Lake. That was mostly because it was close. What I most remember about the spring of my childhood is this Xuanwu Lake. When I was in Nanjing before, I would go almost ten times every spring. Three or four people, a group, buying two or three catties of cherries, a small boat, in the lake, we would sing, chat, talk. The shadow of Zijin Mountain was reflected in the lake in the distance, clear and bright. The sun sprinkled thousands and thousands of golden threads on the trees, the cherries, the soil, the lake, and the heads of the tourists. Far away, in the groves of trees, a parasol moved faintly, and under the parasol was the hem of a skirt being blown by the breeze. A poem, outside Fengrun Gate, permeated with the atmosphere of spring. Donkeys, rickshaws, bicycles, formed a bustling scene. At that time, at that time, I didn't understand anything. What I understood was playing foolishly, eating foolishly, laughing foolishly.

That night, the moon should have been very good, but because the sky was misty, only a pale, dead-man's-face-like color appeared on the big screen. Everything on the lake seemed to have fallen into slumber, so quiet that there wasn't a sound. From Fengrun Gate, the absolutely straight embankment, about three or four meters long, had dense branches on both sides. Under the dense branches, a secluded road unfolded. Leisurely, quiet, unheeded boats floated on the lake like fallen leaves. Occasionally, a bit of fire appeared on a blurred island, as interesting as a star in the sky.

At first, we walked together, in a row, like four soldiers. Later, I wanted to let myself wander alone for a while, saying, "You go ahead a few steps." So I fell behind thirty or forty yards, walking leisurely as if I had disappeared. Sometimes I was muttering some inexplicable lines of poetry, and sometimes I was singing "Lonesome Road" from "Showboat." The atmosphere was very bleak, but because the trip to Beiping made me unspeakably happy, sadness did not attack my heart at all.

VI. A "whoosh" sound suddenly overturned my peaceful heart.

I had booked a ticket for the express train that departed from Pukou at 7:00 p.m. on the third, so at a little after 2:00 p.m. on the third, I hired a car with my nephew, Xi, to go to Xiaguan. The pain in my muscles and bones that had erupted from over-riding horses made me unable to even lift a small suitcase. That time, I was able to cross the river smoothly and get on the train entirely thanks to Xi's help.

That day, the fog was very heavy. Not to mention that you couldn't see Pukou across the river from the riverside of Xiaguan, even in Changzi, I'm afraid that objects beyond ten yards were completely blurred. We took the 3:30 p.m. ferry across the river. Jiangnan, Jiangnan disappeared in that seemingly reluctant-to-parting mood. White gulls occasionally splashed in the water in the heavy fog, and then I didn't know where they flew, to the edge of the sky or the corner of the earth. On the boat, neither Xi nor I said a word. Thus, we arrived at Pukou.

It was hard to find my own berth. The train was a blue-steel train, which I had never had in the South. A small compartment had four berths in total, two upper berths and two lower berths. At that time, the special express from Shanghai had not yet arrived in Nanjing. The train was deserted and a bit scary. Only some porters transporting mail and luggage on the platform were shouting loudly, giving some life to the entire station.

Xi sat in my room for a while, because he had to return to the city, so I advised him to leave. "Seeing a friend off for a thousand miles, there must be a parting." Anyway, I didn't feel any sadness in my heart at that time. He felt that what I said was right, and it wasn't too early in the day. So, I shook his hand, said a few "Farewells," and sent him off the train. I stood on the platform until his figure disappeared in the blur, and then I returned my gaze, neck, and heels to their original state.

At that time, a locomotive was driving into the station from the north end. A "whoosh" sound, it was so sharp, alas, it was so sharp, like a thunderclap, suddenly overturning my peaceful heart. From Shanghai all the way to stepping on the Jinpu train, my breath was always so calm, and it had never been as unbearable as it was at that time. My soul felt like it had been violently shaken, and it floated up a bit. I looked back at the South River hidden in the fog, and walked back to the train car dejectedly.

Spring Night Stroll 201

— Xiao Jun

I. Rouge and Cherry Lips

Was it not cherry blossom season yet? Probably the whole country in the East was madly celebrating the cherry blossom season. I don't know why, but while Rou and I were walking on the road, I thought of cherry blossoms.

My heart has always been saddened by the changes of human affairs, the past like bubbles, and stirred up like the spring breeze ruffling the water in the pond. Although the weather outside was warm, I wanted to run out of the confined room and wander around. Several times I came back seeing people with hateful faces. It's not that I didn't want to be with them, I really was a bit scared of their cleverness, wanting to be a noble and detached person. So I thought like this alone in the room, and that going out would be better to wait until late at night. At night everything is quiet, I can stand on the street watching the dissolving spring night moon, and I can also appreciate the beauty of the moon. The goose-yellow moonlight洒洒 on the city buildings like a large tomb, and heaven and earth return to solemnity and harmony.

Tonight, I swallowed this unprecedented pleasure into my heart with my breath. Ye also accompanied me out of Tangjiawan like a chanting poet. The engines of the machines in the factory were becoming louder. All around was quiet, quiet, only the rising and falling sounds of the machines turning could be heard.

It's so lonely, this spring without flowers, we said lonely. Thinking that the cherry blossoms in Japan are just beautiful now, but we don't have the blessing to see them. Although it is spring here, the street lights are still as dim and yellow as in winter nights, and the feelings they give us on a sensory level don't make us feel spring. On the side of the road, there are still a few sparse young women selling their bodies. Without any brilliance, like a moon about to set but not yet setting, they greeted passers-by with their voices. Next to each young woman was an old woman with ugly temples. We all walked past dejectedly. After passing through many such difficult checkpoints, we were persuaded by one of them at a certain place. Her waist was soft, her eyes were clear, and the color of the rouge on her lips was particularly striking, making people recognize that this was a cherry blossom petal. Ah, cherry blossoms of the East, we indifferently walked away. Cherry blossoms are supposed to be in bloom at night.

II. Night Pounding

Two young people with a slightly decadent air ran from Tangjiawan all the way to the suburbs, discovering a wilderness. There was a small river, dirty and narrow, making people wonder if it was a ditch. Small boats were arranged head to tail in it. We stood on the bank and looked at the half-bright lights in the boats, and could guess that they were not sleeping soundly at this moment, because the moon sometimes flashed into the clouds, and the wilderness immediately seemed to be covered by a net-like fog. The barking of dogs across the wilderness also came to our ears intermittently. The layers of stacked sleepers along the river were also placed there like corpses. This night's scene was a bit desolate and made people shudder. The drooping old branches had not grown their tender buds, nor had they bloomed. We walked leisurely, walked, and Rou and I both felt a little thirsty, wanting to find some water to drink, but the doors of the teahouses were all tightly closed at this time. The water in the river was so dirty. If we could drink it, we would have scooped the water into our hands and drank it long ago. At this time, we really had no choice and didn't speak, just thinking about going to a place to find a source of water. I believe we are in the desert at this moment.

Home
